A number of books ably cover the entirety of the Cold War. Particularly recommended are David S. Painter, [3mThe Cold War: An 
International History [0m(London, 1999); Martin Walker, [3mThe Cold War: A History [0m(London, 1993); S. J. Ball, [3mThe Cold War: An 
International History, 1947โ1991 [0m(London, 1998); Richard J. Crockatt, [3mThe Fifty Years War: The United States and the Soviet Union 
in World Politics, 1941โ1991 [0m(London, 1995); Walter LaFeber, [3mAmerica, Russia, and the Cold War, 1945โ2000, [0m9th edn. (New York, 
2002); Ronald E. Powaski, [3mThe Cold War: The United States and the Soviet Union, 1917โ1991 [0m(New York, 1998); Geoffrey Roberts, [3mThe 
Soviet Union in World Politics: Coexistence, Revolution and Cold War, 1945โ1991 [0m(London, 1999); Thomas J. McCormick, [3mAmericaโs 
Half-Century: United States Foreign Policy in the Cold War [0m(Baltimore, 1989); Warren I. Cohen, [3mAmerica in the Age of Soviet Power, 
1945โ1991 [0m(New York, 1993); and H. W. Brands, [3mThe Devil We Knew: Americans and the Cold War [0m(New York, 1993). 

Important works that utilize new archival sources to reinterpret the first half of the Cold War include Vladislav Zubok and 
Constantine Pleshakov, [3mInside the Kremlinโs Cold War: From Stalin to Khrushchev [0m(Cambridge, Mass., 1996) and John Lewis Gaddis, [3mWe 
Now Know: Rethinking Cold War History [0m(Oxford, 1997). A useful collection is Odd Arne Westad (ed.), [3mReviewing the Cold War: 
Approaches, Interpretations, Theory [0m(London, 2000).
